      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_system">
        Traditional system
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Venetian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Traditional system">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Venetian does not have an
       <a href="/wiki/Official_script" title="Official script">
        official writing system
       </a>
       , but it is traditionally written using the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">
        Latin script
       </a>
       — sometimes with certain additional letters or diacritics. The basis for some of these conventions can be traced to Old Venetian, while others are purely modern innovations.
      </p>
      <p>
       Medieval texts, written in Old Venetian, include the letters ⟨x⟩, ⟨ç⟩ and ⟨z⟩ to represent sounds that do not exist or have a different distribution in Italian. Specifically:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The letter ⟨x⟩ was often employed in words that nowadays have a voiced
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
          z
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        -sound (compare English
        <i>
         xylophone
        </i>
        ); for instance ⟨x⟩ appears in words such as
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          raxon
         </span>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          Croxe
         </span>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          caxa
         </span>
        </i>
        ("reason", "(holy) Cross" and "house"). The precise phonetic value of ⟨x⟩ in Old Venetian texts remains unknown, however.
       </li>
       <li>
        The letter ⟨z⟩ often appeared in words that nowadays have a varying voiced pronunciation ranging from
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
          z
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        to
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_sibilant_affricate" title="Voiced alveolar sibilant affricate">
          dz
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        or
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_fricative" title="Voiced dental fricative">
          ð
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        or even to
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Alveolar" title="Voiced dental and alveolar stops">
          d
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        ; even in contemporary spelling
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          zo
         </span>
        </i>
        "down" may represent any of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /zo, dzo, ðo/
        </span>
        or even
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /do/
        </span>
        , depending on the dialect; similarly
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          zovena
         </span>
        </i>
        "young woman" could be any of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈzovena/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈdzovena/
        </span>
        or
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈðovena/
        </span>
        , and
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          zero
         </span>
        </i>
        "zero" could be
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈzɛro/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈdzɛro/
        </span>
        or
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈðɛro/
        </span>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Likewise, ⟨ç⟩ was written for a voiceless sound which now varies, depending on the dialect spoken, from
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">
          s
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        to
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar sibilant affricate">
          ts
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        to
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_fricative" title="Voiceless dental fricative">
          θ
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        , as in for example
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          dolçe
         </span>
        </i>
        "sweet", now
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈdolse ~ ˈdoltse ~ ˈdolθe/
        </span>
        ,
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          dolçeça
         </span>
        </i>
        "sweetness", now
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dolˈsesa ~ dolˈtsetsa ~ dolˈθeθa/
        </span>
        , or
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          sperança
         </span>
        </i>
        "hope", now
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /speˈransa ~ speˈrantsa ~ speˈranθa/
        </span>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The usage of letters in medieval and early modern texts was not, however, entirely consistent. In particular, as in other northern Italian languages, the letters ⟨z⟩ and ⟨ç⟩ were often used interchangeably for both voiced and voiceless sounds. Differences between earlier and modern pronunciation, divergences in pronunciation within the modern Venetian-speaking region, differing attitudes about how closely to model spelling on Italian norms, as well as personal preferences, some of which reflect sub-regional identities, have all hindered the adoption of a single unified spelling system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nevertheless, in practice, most spelling conventions are the same as in Italian. In some early modern texts letter ⟨x⟩ becomes limited to word-initial position, as in
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         xe
        </span>
       </i>
       ("is"), where its use was unavoidable because Italian spelling cannot represent
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
         z
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       there. In between vowels, the distinction between
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">
         s
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
         z
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       was ordinarily indicated by doubled ⟨ss⟩ for the former and single ⟨s⟩ for the latter. For example,
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         basa
        </span>
       </i>
       was used to represent
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈbaza/
       </span>
       ("he/she kisses"), whereas
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         bassa
        </span>
       </i>
       represented
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈbasa/
       </span>
       ("low"). (Before consonants there is no contrast between
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">
         s
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
         z
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       , as in Italian, so a single ⟨s⟩ is always used in this circumstance, it being understood that the ⟨s⟩ will agree in voicing with the following consonant. For example, ⟨st⟩ represents only
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /st/
       </span>
       , but ⟨sn⟩ represents
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /zn/
       </span>
       .)
      </p>
      <p>
       Traditionally the letter ⟨z⟩ was ambiguous, having the same values as in Italian (both voiced and voiceless affricates
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_sibilant_affricate" title="Voiced alveolar sibilant affricate">
         dz
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar sibilant affricate">
         ts
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ). Nevertheless, in some books the two pronunciations are sometimes distinguished (in between vowels at least) by using doubled ⟨zz⟩ to indicate
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar sibilant affricate">
         ts
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       (or in some dialects
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_fricative" title="Voiceless dental fricative">
         θ
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ) but a single ⟨z⟩ for
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_sibilant_affricate" title="Voiced alveolar sibilant affricate">
         dz
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       (or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_fricative" title="Voiced dental fricative">
         ð
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Alveolar" title="Voiced dental and alveolar stops">
         d
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       In more recent practice the use of ⟨x⟩ to represent
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
         z
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       , both in word-initial as well as in intervocalic contexts, has become increasingly common, but no entirely uniform convention has emerged for the representation of the voiced vs. voiceless affricates (or interdental fricatives), although a return to using ⟨ç⟩ and ⟨z⟩ remains an option under consideration.
      </p>
      <p>
       Regarding the spelling of the vowel sounds, because in Venetian, as in Italian, there is no contrast between tense and lax vowels in unstressed syllables, the orthographic grave and acute accents can be used to mark both stress and vowel quality at the same time:
       <i>
        à
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">
         a
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        á
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Near-open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open central unrounded vowel">
         ɐ
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        è
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">
         ɛ
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        é
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">
         e
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        ò
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">
         ɔ
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        ó
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">
         o
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        ù
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">
         u
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       . Different orthographic norms prescribe slightly different rules for when stressed vowels must be written with accents or may be left unmarked, and no single system has been accepted by all speakers.
      </p>
      <p>
       Venetian allows the
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant_cluster" title="Consonant cluster">
        consonant cluster
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /stʃ/
       </span>
       (not present in Italian), which is sometimes written ⟨s-c⟩ or ⟨s'c⟩ before
       <i>
        i
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       , and ⟨s-ci⟩ or ⟨s'ci⟩ before other vowels. Examples include
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         s-ciarir
        </span>
       </i>
       (Italian
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         schiarire
        </span>
       </i>
       , "to clear up"),
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         s-cèt
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         schietto
        </span>
       </i>
       , "plain clear"),
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         s-ciòp
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         schioppo
        </span>
       </i>
       , "gun") and
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         s-ciao
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         schiavo
        </span>
       </i>
       , "[your] servant",
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         ciao
        </span>
       </i>
       , "hello", "goodbye"). The hyphen or apostrophe is used because the combination ⟨sc(i)⟩ is conventionally used for the
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">
         ʃ
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       sound, as in Italian spelling; e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         scèmo
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         scemo
        </span>
       </i>
       , "stupid"); whereas ⟨sc⟩ before
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        u
       </i>
       represents
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /sk/
       </span>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         scàtoła
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         scatola
        </span>
       </i>
       , "box"),
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         scóndar
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         nascondere
        </span>
       </i>
       , "to hide"),
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         scusàr
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
         scusare
        </span>
       </i>
       , "to forgive").
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_systems">
        Proposed systems
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Venetian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Proposed systems">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Recently there have been attempts to standardize and simplify the script by reusing older letters, e.g. by using ⟨x⟩ for
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
         z
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       and a single ⟨s⟩ for
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">
         s
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       ; then one would write
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         baxa
        </span>
       </i>
       for
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Venetian" title="Help:IPA/Venetian">
         [ˈbaza]
        </a>
       </span>
       ("[third person singular] kisses") and
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         basa
        </span>
       </i>
       for
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Venetian" title="Help:IPA/Venetian">
         [ˈbasa]
        </a>
       </span>
       ("low"). Some authors have continued or resumed the use of ⟨ç⟩, but only when the resulting word is not too different from the Italian orthography: in modern Venetian writings, it is then easier to find words as
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         çima
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         çento
        </span>
       </i>
       , rather than
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         força
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         sperança
        </span>
       </i>
       , even though all these four words display the same phonological variation in the position marked by the letter ⟨ç⟩. Another recent convention is to use ⟨ł⟩ for the "soft"
       <i>
        l
       </i>
       , to allow a more unified orthography for all variants of the language. However, in spite of their theoretical advantages, these proposals have not been very successful outside of academic circles, because of regional variations in pronunciation and incompatibility with existing literature.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Venetian speakers of
       <a href="/wiki/Chipilo" title="Chipilo">
        Chipilo
       </a>
       use a system based on Spanish orthography, even though it does not contain letters for
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Palatal_approximant#Palatal" title="Palatal approximant">
         j
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_fricative" title="Voiceless dental fricative">
         θ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       . The American linguist Carolyn McKay proposed a writing system for that variant, based entirely on the
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       alphabet. However, the system was not very popular.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_texts">
        Sample texts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Venetian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sample texts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ruzante_returning_from_war">
        Ruzante returning from war
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Venetian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ruzante returning from war">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The following sample, in the old dialect of Padua, comes from a play by Ruzante (
       <a href="/wiki/Angelo_Beolco" title="Angelo Beolco">
        Angelo Beolco
       </a>
       ), titled
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Parlamento_de_Ruzante_che_iera_vegn%C3%B9_de_campo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Parlamento de Ruzante che iera vegnù de campo (page does not exist)">
          Parlamento de Ruzante che iera vegnù de campo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("Dialogue of Ruzante who came from the battlefield", 1529). The character, a peasant returning home from the war, is expressing to his friend Menato his relief at being still alive:
      </p>
      <div>
       <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:auto;">
        <tr>
         <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
          <div class="poem" style="font-variant: italic; margin-left: 1em;">
           <p>
            <i>
             <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
              Orbéntena, el no serae mal
              <br/>
              star in campo per sto robare,
              <br/>
              se 'l no foesse che el se ha pur
              <br/>
              de gran paure. Càncaro ala roba!
              <br/>
              A' son chialò mi, ala segura,
              <br/>
              e squase che no a' no cherzo
              <br/>
              esserghe gnan. [...]
              <br/>
              Se mi mo' no foesse mi?
              <br/>
              E che a foesse stò amazò in campo?
              <br/>
              E che a foesse el me spirito?
              <br/>
              Lo sarae ben bela.
              <br/>
              No, càncaro, spiriti no magna.
             </span>
            </i>
           </p>
          </div>
         </td>
         <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top; padding-left: 2em;">
          <div class="poem" style="margin-left: 1em;">
           <p>
            "Really, it would not be that bad
            <br/>
            to be in the battlefield looting,
            <br/>
            were it not that one gets also
            <br/>
            big scares. Damn the loot!
            <br/>
            I am right here, in safety,
            <br/>
            and almost can't believe
            <br/>
            I am. [...]
            <br/>
            And if I were not me?
            <br/>
            And if I had been killed in battle?
            <br/>
            And if I were my ghost?
            <br/>
            That would be just great.
            <br/>
            No, damn, ghosts don't eat."
           </p>
          </div>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Discorso_de_Perasto">
        <i>
         <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
          Discorso de Perasto
         </span>
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Venetian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Discorso de Perasto">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The following sample is taken from the
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Perasto_Speech&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Perasto Speech (page does not exist)">
         Perasto Speech
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
         Discorso de Perasto
        </span>
       </i>
       ), given on August 23, 1797 at
       <a href="/wiki/Perast" title="Perast">
        Perasto
       </a>
       , by Venetian Captain
       <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Viscovich" title="Giuseppe Viscovich">
        Giuseppe Viscovich
       </a>
       , at the last lowering of the flag of the Venetian Republic (nicknamed the "Republic of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Mark%27s_Cathedral,_Venice" title="St Mark's Cathedral, Venice">
        Saint Mark
       </a>
       ").
      </p>
      <div>
       <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:auto;">
        <tr>
         <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
          <div class="poem" style="font-variant: italic; margin-left: 1em;">
           <p>
            <i>
             <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
              Par trezentosetantasete ani
              <br/>
              le nostre sostanse, el nostro sangue,
              <br/>
              le nostre vite le xè sempre stàe
              <br/>
              par Ti, S. Marco; e fedelisimi
              <br/>
              senpre se gavemo reputà,
              <br/>
              Ti co nu, nu co Ti,
              <br/>
              e sempre co Ti sul mar
              <br/>
              semo stài lustri e virtuosi.
              <br/>
              Nisun co Ti ne gà visto scanpar,
              <br/>
              nisun co Ti ne gà visto vinti e spaurosi!
             </span>
            </i>
           </p>
          </div>
         </td>
         <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top; padding-left: 2em;">
          <div class="poem">
           <p>
            "For three hundred and seventy seven years
            <br/>
            our bodies, our blood
            <br/>
            our lives have always been
            <br/>
            for You, St. Mark; and very faithful
            <br/>
            we have always thought ourselves,
            <br/>
            You with us, we with You,
            <br/>
            And always with You on the sea
            <br/>
            we have been illustrious and virtuous.
            <br/>
            No one has seen us with You flee,
            <br/>
            No one has seen us with You defeated and fearful!"
           </p>
          </div>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Francesco_Artico">
        Francesco Artico
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Venetian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Francesco Artico">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The following is a contemporary text by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Francesco_Artico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Francesco Artico (page does not exist)">
        Francesco Artico
       </a>
       . The elderly narrator is recalling the church choir singers of his youth, who, needless to say, sang much better than those of today:
      </p>
      <div>
       <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:auto;">
        <tr>
         <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
          <div class="poem" style="font-variant: italic; margin-left: 1em;">
           <p>
            <i>
             <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
              Sti cantori vèci da na volta,
              <br/>
              co i cioéa su le profezie,
              <br/>
              in mezo al coro, davanti al restèl,
              <br/>
              co'a ose i 'ndéa a cior volta
              <br/>
              no so 'ndove e ghe voéa un bèl tóc
              <br/>
              prima che i tornésse in qua
              <br/>
              e che i rivésse in cao,
              <br/>
              màssima se i jèra pareciàdi onti
              <br/>
              co mezo litro de quel bon
              <br/>
              tant par farse coràjo.
             </span>
            </i>
           </p>
          </div>
         </td>
         <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top; padding-left: 2em;">
          <div class="poem">
           <p>
            "These old singers of the past,
            <br/>
            when they picked up the Prophecies,
            <br/>
            in the middle of the choir, in front of the gate,
            <br/>
            with their voice they went off
            <br/>
            who knows where, and it was a long time
            <br/>
            before they came back
            <br/>
            and landed on the ground,
            <br/>
            especially if they had been previously 'oiled'
            <br/>
            with half a litre of the good one [wine]
            <br/>
            just to make courage."
           </p>
          </div>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="English_cognates_with_Venetian">
        English cognates with Venetian
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [

        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           arsenàl
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Arsenal" title="Arsenal">
          arsenal
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         via Italian; from Arabic
         <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
          دار الصناعة
         </span>
         <i>
          dār al-ṣināʻah
         </i>
         "house of manufacture, factory"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           artichioco / articiòco
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Artichoke" title="Artichoke">
          artichoke
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         from Arabic
         <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
          الخرشوف
         </span>
         <i>
          al-kharshūf
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           balòta
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Ballot" title="Ballot">
          ballot
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         ball used in Venetian elections; cf. English to "black-ball"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           casìn
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">
          casino
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         "little house"; adopted in Italianized form
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           s'ciào
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Ciao" title="Ciao">
          ciao
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         cognate with Italian
         <i>
          <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
           schiavo
          </span>
         </i>
         "slave"; used originally in Venetian to mean "your servant", "at your service"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           contrabando
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Contraband" title="Contraband">
          contraband
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           gazéta
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Gazette" title="Gazette">
          gazette
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         a small Venetian coin; from the phrase
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           gazeta de la novità
          </span>
         </i>
         "a pennysworth of news"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           g(h)èto
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Ghetto" title="Ghetto">
          ghetto
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         hypothesized as from either
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           (bor)ghetto
          </span>
         </i>
         "little city", or from the Venetian term for "foundry"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           ziro
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Giro" title="Giro">
          giro
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         "circle, turn, spin"; adopted in Italianized form; from the name of the bank
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           Banco del Ziro
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           gnòco, -chi
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Gnocchi" title="Gnocchi">
          gnocchi
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         lump, bump, gnocchi; from Germanic *
         <i>
          knokk
         </i>
         - 'knuckle, joint'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           góndoła
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Gondola" title="Gondola">
          gondola
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         possibly related to
         <i>
          <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
           dondolare
          </span>
         </i>
         "to rock"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">

         </a>
        </td>

         <i>

           lacus
          </span>

         "lake"
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           lazaréto
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Lazaretto" title="Lazaretto">
          Lazaretto
         </a>
         , lazaret
        </td>
        <td>
         a quarantine station for maritime travellers, ultimately from the Biblical
         <a href="/wiki/Lazarus_of_Bethany" title="Lazarus of Bethany">
          Lazarus of Bethany
         </a>
         , who was raised from the dead
        </td>
       </tr>

           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Lido" title="Lido">
          lido
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>

         <i>
          <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
           litus
          </span>

        </td>

       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>

           lò(t)to
          </span>

        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Lottery" title="Lottery">
          lotto
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         from Germanic *
         <i>
          lot
         </i>
         - "destiny, fate"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           malvasìa
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malmsey" title="Malmsey">
          malmsey
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         ultimately from the name
         <a href="/wiki/Monemvasia" title="Monemvasia">
          Monemvasia
         </a>
         , a small Greek island off the Peloponnese once owned by the Venetian Republic and a source of strong, sweet white wine from Greece and the eastern Mediterranean
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           marzapàn
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Marzipan" title="Marzipan">
          marzipan
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         from the name for the porcelain container in which marzipan was transported, from Arabic
         <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
          موثبان
         </span>
         <i>
          mawthabān
         </i>
         , or from
         <a href="/wiki/Mottama" title="Mottama">
          Mataban
         </a>
         in the
         <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">
          Bay of Bengal
         </a>
         where these were made (these are some of several proposed etymologies for the English word)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="vec" xml:lang="vec">
           Negropónte
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Euboea" title="Euboea">
          Negroponte
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Greek island called Euboea or Evvia in the
         <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">
          Aegean Sea
         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Quarantine" title="Quarantine">
          quarantine
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         "forty", referring to the number of days a ship with plague victims must remain isolated
        </td>

        </td>

         </a>

         from Greek
         <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BA%CE%AC%CE%BC%CF%80%CE%B7#Greek" title="wikt:κάμπη">

           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=International+The+other+Italy%3A+the+literary+canon+in+dialect&amp;rft.place=Toronto&amp;rft.date=1999&amp;rft.aulast=Haller&amp;rft.aufirst=Hermann+W.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVenetian+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-Renzi-16">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-Renzi_16-0">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation book">
            Renzi, Lorenzo (1994).
            <i>
             Nuova introduzione alla filologia romanza
            </i>
            . Bologna: Il Mulino. p. 176.
            <q>
             <i>
              <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
               I dialetti settentrionali formano un blocco abbastanza compatto con molti tratti comuni che li accostano, oltre che tra loro, qualche volta anche alla parlate cosiddette ladine e alle lingue galloromanze ... Alcuni fenomeni morfologici innovativi sono pure abbastanza largamente comuni, come la doppia serie pronominale soggetto (non sempre in tutte le persone) ... Ma più spesso il veneto si distacca dal gruppo, lasciando così da una parte tutti gli altri dialetti, detti gallo-italici.
              </span>
             </i>
            </q>
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Nuova+introduzione+alla+filologia+romanza&amp;rft.place=Bologna&amp;rft.pages=176&amp;rft.pub=Il+Mulino&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.aulast=Renzi&amp;rft.aufirst=Lorenzo&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVenetian+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-17">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-17">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Alberto Zamboni(1988:522)
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-18">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-18">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Giovan Battista Pellegrini (1976:425)
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-zamboni-19">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-zamboni_19-0">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation book">
            Zamboni, Alberto (1975). Cortelazzo, Manlio, ed.
            <i>
             Veneto
            </i>
            [
            <i>
             Venetian language
            </i>
            ]. Profilo dei dialetti italiani (in Italian).
            <b>
             5
            </b>
            . Pisa: Pacini. p. 12.
            <q>
             <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">
              b) n a s a l i: esistono, come nello 'standard', 3 fonemi, /m/, /n/, /ń/, immediatamente identificabili da /
              <i>
               mása
              </i>
              / 'troppo' ~ /
              <i>
               nása
              </i>
              / 'nasca'; /
              <i>
               manáse
              </i>
              / 'manacce' ~ /
              <i>
               mańáse
              </i>
              / 'mangiasse', ecc., come, rispettivamente, bilabiale, apicodentale, palatale; per quanto riguarda gli allòfoni e la loro distribuzione, è da notare [
              <i>
               ṅ
              </i>
              ] dorsovelare, cfr. [
              <i>
               áṅka
              </i>
              ] 'anche', e, regolarmente in posizione finale: [
              <i>
               parọ́ṅ
              </i>
              ] 'padrone', [
              <i>
               britoíṅ
              </i>
              ] 'temperino': come questa, è caratteristica v e n e t a la realizzazione velare anche davanti a cons. d'altro tipo, cfr. [
              <i>
               kaṅtár
              </i>
              ], it. [
              <i>
               kantáre
              </i>
              ]; [
              <i>
               iṅvę́rno
              </i>
              ], it. [
              <i>
               iɱvę́rno
              </i>
              ]; [
              <i>
               ọ́ṅʃar
              </i>
              ] 'ungere', [
              <i>
               raṅǧárse
              </i>
              ], it. [
              <i>
               arrańǧársi
              </i>
              ], ecc.
             </span>
            </q>
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Veneto&amp;rft.place=Pisa&amp;rft.series=Profilo+dei+dialetti+italiani&amp;rft.pages=12&amp;rft.pub=Pacini&amp;rft.date=1975&amp;rft.aulast=Zamboni&amp;rft.aufirst=Alberto&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVenetian+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
